to carry on as a platform of diverse music, Zorlu PSM is always on the look-out for presenting renown musicians from around the world to its audience. Tinariwen, the group composed of Tuareg musicians from the Sahara Desert region of northern Mali, is coming to Zorlu PSM on March 22, 2017.    Ibrahim Ag Alhabib, the founder of the group, started to take an interest in music at childhood after seeing a cowboy playing a guitar in a Western movie. Creating a guitar from the different objects he brought together, he started to play traditional Tuareg songs and Arabic pop songs. Tinariwen started to play the guitar as well as other traditional instruments in refugee camps in 1979. They were influenced by legends such as Elvis Presley, Led Zeppelin, Carlos Santana, Dire Straits, Jimi Hendrix, Boney M and Bob Marley, along with Moroccan protest groups such as Nass El Ghiwane and Jil Jilala.  Having released 6 albums throughout its career, the last one being Emmaar in 2014, Tinariwen has succeeded in bringing its musical journey to esteemed festival stages such as Glastonbury, Roskilde and Coachella. After the 2004 album Amassakoul was released, the group received the BBC World Music Award in 2005.  In the 2010s, Tinariwen gained further success by taking the stage during the opening ceremonies of World Cup 2010 in South Africa and receiving a Grammy for Best World Music with its album titled Tassili in 2012. The group has ever-changing members and a massive fanbase that includes Carlos Santana, Robert Plant, Bono and the Edge from U2, Thom Yorke, Chris Marin, Henry Rollins, Brian Eno and TV On The Radio. Tinariwen is accompanied by talented musicians during album recordings and live performances. Josh Klinghoffer, Fats Kaplin, Matt Sweeney and Saul Williams are some world renown musicians who accompany them besides local musicians.  One of the most important factors that set Tinariwen apart is their high energy and captivating live performances. Harmonizing the North African Tishoumaren music with blues, rock and folk, Tinariwen has proven to be one of the most authentic artists of world music and carries this uniqueness to the stage. Montreux Jazz FestivalMontreux Jazz Festival takes places over 2 weeks each summer in Switzerland on the shores of Lake Geneva. The Montreux Jazz Festival was created in 1967 by Claude Nobs, Ren Langel, and Go Voumard, and has since become a landmark event.Not because it draws more than 250,000 visitors, or because those two weeks in Montreux make up one of the best-known events in Europe and beyond, but rather because the Festival has kept its soul intact throughout all this growth.At Montreux, the intimacy that encourages improvisation remains a top priority.Proximity between the biggest artists and their audiences in concert halls of reasonable capacity, comfortable surroundings, and a quality listening experience all combine to produce unique concerts and encourage memorable moments.While jazz and blues are at the roots of this event, other styles of music quickly found their place as well, anchored by artistic encounters between generations of musicians and unique experiments.Montreux has seen historic performances by artists including Nina Simone, Miles Davis, Ella Fitzgerald, Marvin Gaye, Prince, Leonard Cohen, David Bowie, and Stevie Wonder.The three ticketed venues (Auditorium Stravinski, Montreux Jazz Club, Montreux Jazz Lab) showcase the Festivals prestigious lineup of artists.However, from the very beginning Festival founder Claude Nobs wanted to offer access to music to everyone, and so a wide variety of free programming energizes the Festival site and provides opportunities for emerging artists to shine.Kicking off each afternoon with the open-air stage of Music in the Park and the workshops, and continuing until the wee hours with the Rock Cave and various after-show events, the Festival ambiance is in full swing on the lakefront promenades with their rich variety of food stands and on the terraces by the lake with their inimitable Alpine
